# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've successfully identified and documented all the Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the consumer group coordinator's state machine. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings:

**25 Java files** implementing the consumer group coordinator state machine:

### Classic Protocol (JoinGroup/SyncGroup)
- **ClassicGroupState.java** - Defines 5 states: EMPTY, PREPARING_REBALANCE, COMPLETING_REBALANCE, STABLE, DEAD
- **ClassicGroup.java** - Implements state transitions via `transitionTo()` method
- **ClassicGroupMember.java** - Represents classic protocol group members

### Modern Consumer Protocol (ConsumerGroupHeartbeat)
- **ConsumerGroup.java** - Defines states: EMPTY, ASSIGNING, RECONCILING, STABLE, DEAD
- **modern/MemberState.java** - Member-level states: STABLE, UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS, UNRELEASED_PARTITIONS
- **CurrentAssignmentBuilder.java** - Reconciliation engine for converging member/target assignment
- **TargetAssignmentBuilder.java** - Builds target assignments

### Streams & Share Protocols
- **StreamsGroup.java**, **streams/MemberState.java** - Stream processing group management
- **ShareGroup.java**, **ShareGroupMember.java** - Share group protocol support

### Coordinator Components
- **GroupMetadataManager.java** - Core state orchestration with `classicGroupJoin()`, `classicGroupSync()`, `consumerGroupHeartbeat()`
- **GroupCoordinatorShard.java**, **GroupCoordinatorService.java** - Request handling layers
- **GroupCoordinatorRecordHelpers.java** - Record creation utilities

### Client-Side
- **clients/.../MemberState.java** - Client-side states: UNSUBSCRIBED, JOINING, RECONCILING, ACKNOWLEDGING, STABLE, FENCED, etc.

consumer group coordinator state machine is implemented across multiple Java files in the apache/kafka repository (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489). The implementation includes two major protocol versions: the classic (JoinGroup/SyncGroup) protocol and the modern (ConsumerGroupHeartbeat) protocol.\\n\\n## Classic Group Protocol State Machine\\n\\nThe classic group state machine is defined in **ClassicGroupState.java** with five states:\\n1. **EMPTY** - Group has no members, lingers until offsets expire\\n2. **PREPARING_REBALANCE** - Group is preparing to rebalance after a join group request\\n3. **COMPLETING_REBALANCE** - Group awaits leader's assignment via SyncGroup\\n4. **STABLE** - Group is stable and members are active\\n5. **DEAD** - Final state before cleanup\\n\\nThe state transitions are validated in **ClassicGroup.java** through the `transitionTo()` method and `assertValidTransition()` method. The transitions follow defined rules (e.g., PREPARING_REBALANCE can transition from STABLE, COMPLETING_REBALANCE, or EMPTY).\\n\\n## Modern Consumer Group Protocol State Machine\\n\\nThe modern consumer group uses:\\n- **ConsumerGroupState** enum in **ConsumerGroup.java** with states: EMPTY, ASSIGNING, RECONCILING, STABLE, DEAD\\n- **MemberState** enum in **modern/MemberState.java** with member-level states: STABLE, UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS, UNRELEASED_PARTITIONS, UNKNOWN\\n\\nThe reconciliation logic is implemented in **CurrentAssignmentBuilder.java**, which encapsulates the reconciliation engine that converges member state with target assignment state.\\n\\n## Streams Group Protocol State Machine\\n\\nStreams groups are defined in **StreamsGroup.java** and **streams/MemberState.java**, implementing similar state management for stream processing topology assignments.\\n\\n## Client-Side State Machine\\n\\nThe client-side member state machine is defined in **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/MemberState.java** with states: UNSUBSCRIBED, JOINING, RECONCILING, ACKNOWLEDGING, STABLE, FENCED, PREPARE_LEAVING, LEAVING, FATAL, STALE.\\n\\n## Main Coordinator Components\\n\\nThe state machine is managed through:\\n- **GroupMetadataManager.java** - Contains `classicGroupJoin()`, `classicGroupSync()`, and `consumerGroupHeartbeat()` methods that orchestrate state transitions\\n- **GroupCoordinatorShard.java** - Request handler interface\\n- **GroupCoordinatorService.java** - Service layer for coordinator operations\\n- **GroupCoordinator.java** - Top-level coordinator interface\\n- **GroupCoordinatorRecordHelpers.java** - Helper functions for creating coordinator records\\n\\n## Target Assignment Builders\\n\\nThe assignment process uses:\\n- **TargetAssignmentBuilder.java** (modern consumer and streams) - Builds target assignments for groups\\n- **ShareGroupAssignmentBuilder.java** - For share groups\\n\\nThe Join, Sync, and Rebalance operations are implemented through the interaction of these components, with state transitions recorded as CoordinatorRecords in the __consumer_offsets topic.\"\n}\n",

The implementation includes two major protocol versions: the classic (JoinGroup/SyncGroup) protocol and the modern (ConsumerGroupHeartbeat) protocol.\\n\\n## Classic Group Protocol State Machine\\n\\nThe classic group state machine is defined in **ClassicGroupState.java** with five states:\\n1. **EMPTY** - Group has no members, lingers until offsets expire\\n2. **PREPARING_REBALANCE** - Group is preparing to rebalance after a join group request\\n3. **COMPLETING_REBALANCE** - Group awaits leader's assignment via SyncGroup\\n4. **STABLE** - Group is stable and members are active\\n5. **DEAD** - Final state before cleanup\\n\\nThe state transitions are validated in **ClassicGroup.java** through the `transitionTo()` method and `assertValidTransition()` method. The transitions follow defined rules (e.g., PREPARING_REBALANCE can transition from STABLE, COMPLETING_REBALANCE, or EMPTY).\\n\\n## Modern Consumer Group Protocol State Machine\\n\\nThe modern consumer group uses:\\n- **ConsumerGroupState** enum in **ConsumerGroup.java** with states: EMPTY, ASSIGNING, RECONCILING, STABLE, DEAD\\n- **MemberState** enum in **modern/MemberState.java** with member-level states: STABLE, UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS, UNRELEASED_PARTITIONS, UNKNOWN\\n\\nThe reconciliation logic is implemented in **CurrentAssignmentBuilder.java**, which encapsulates the reconciliation engine that converges member state with target assignment state.\\n\\n## Streams Group Protocol State Machine\\n\\nStreams groups are defined in **StreamsGroup.java** and **streams/MemberState.java**, implementing similar state management for stream processing topology assignments.\\n\\n## Client-Side State Machine\\n\\nThe client-side member state machine is defined in **clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/MemberState.java** with states: UNSUBSCRIBED, JOINING, RECONCILING, ACKNOWLEDGING, STABLE, FENCED, PREPARE_LEAVING, LEAVING, FATAL, STALE.\\n\\n## Main Coordinator Components\\n\\nThe state machine is managed through:\\n- **GroupMetadataManager.java** -
